Mathematics, computing and the scientific method
September 12, 2023
Table of Contents

Mathematics, computing and the scientific method as a guide to high-performance software development decisions.
Contextualization
Methods
Consequences
Mathematics, computing and the scientific method as a guide to high-performance software development decisions.
Contextualization
Let's say I have to find the greatest distance, given that these distances are relative to a central point, and several other points.

In other words, given {P0, P1, P2, â¦, Pn}, and considering the distances {P0P1, P0P2, â¦, P0Pn}, what is the greatest distance in this set of distances?

Methods
Using the exhaustion method, we can make a combination of n.(n-1)/2 comparisons. Hey, P0P1 and P0P2, P0P1 and P0P3 etc.

However, we could order the set of distances, and then choose the last (or first). Which will be the biggest. This is in the order of n.log(n) comparisons.

Consequences
Stupid things like that can be the difference between a customer spending 10 minutes, or 1 minute on your website; in addition to satisfaction and willingness to return vary correspondingly.

Butâ¦ Nobody creates a service to calculate distance between points!

No, no... it could be that the best investment for the citizen's profile is being ordered. Or, the bank credit note. Or even part of an algorithm to calculate the best route for a vehicle. Etc.

The study of algorithms is fundamental, accompanied by data structure.

Codes which have algorithms using brute force, which are repetitive and, consequently, inelegant - in addition to becoming a huge technical debt - reduce customer satisfaction.

Stupid things like that can be the difference between a customer spending 10 minutes, or 1 minute on your website; in addition to satisfaction and willingness to return vary correspondingly.

Codes which have algorithms using brute force, which are repetitive and, consequently, inelegant - in addition to becoming a huge technical debt - reduce customer satisfaction.

Dam massacre 2017
The U.S. military bombed a massive Euphrates River dam in Syria in 2017 despite a military report warning such an attack could lead to a flood that would kill tens of thousands of civilians. Thatâs according to The New York Times, which reports the attack on the 18-story Tabqa Dam led to critical equipment failure, causing a reservoir to rise and prompting panicked evacuations downstream. At the time, the commander of the U.S. offensive dismissed reports that the U.S. was responsible as âcrazy reporting.â In fact, the U.S. was responsible, and even selected at least one concrete-penetrating bunker-buster bomb for the attack. A follow-up U.S. airstrike reportedly killed three workers who rushed to the dam to prevent a disaster.

\documentclass[letterpaper]{../cls/twentysecondcvenglish} % a4paper for A4
\usepackage{hyperref}

% Definitions of Pinyin
\makeatletter
\def\py@yunpriv#1{%
  \if a#1 10\else
  \if o#1 9\else
  \if e#1 8\else
  \if i#1 7\else
  \if u#1 6\else
  \if v#1 5\else
  \if A#1 4\else
  \if O#1 3\else
  \if E#1 2\fi\fi\fi\fi\fi\fi\fi\fi\fi0
}

\def\py@init{%
  \edef\py@befirst{}%
  \edef\py@char{}\edef\py@tuneletter{}%
  \def\py@last{}%
  \def\py@tune{5}%
}

% Usage:
% \pinyin{Hao3hao3\ xue2xi2} ï¼å¥½å¥½å­¦ä¹ ï¼
\def\pinyin#1{%
  \edef\py@postscan{#1}%
  \py@init
  % scan
  \loop
  \edef\py@char{\expandafter\@car\py@postscan\@nil}%
  \edef\py@postscan{\expandafter\@cdr\py@postscan\@nil}%
  \ifnum 0 < 0\py@char
    \edef\py@tune{\py@char}%
    \py@first \py@tuneat\py@tuneletter\py@tune \py@last\kern -4sp\kern 4sp{}\py@init
  \else
    \ifnum\py@yunpriv\py@char > \py@yunpriv\py@tuneletter
      \edef\py@tuneletter{\py@char}\edef\py@first{\py@befirst}\def\py@last{}%
    \else
      \edef\py@last{\py@last\if v\py@char\"u\else\py@char\fi}%
    \fi
    \edef\py@befirst{\py@befirst\if v\py@char\"u\else\py@char\fi}%
  \fi
  \ifx\py@postscan\@empty\else
  \repeat
}

\let\py@macron \=
\let\py@acute \'
\let\py@hacek \v
\let\py@grave \`

%% \py@tuneat{Letter}{tune}
\def\py@tuneat#1#2{%
  \if v#1%
    \py@tune@v #2%
  \else
  \if i#1%
    \py@tune@i #2%
  \else
    \ifcase#2%
      \or\py@macron #1\or\py@acute #1\or\py@hacek #1\or\py@grave #1\else #1%
    \fi
  \fi\fi
}

\def\py@tune@v#1{{%
    \dimen@ii 1ex%
    \fontdimen5\font 1.1ex%
    \rlap{\"u}%
    \fontdimen5\font .6ex%
    \ifcase#1%
      \or\py@macron u\or\py@acute u\or\py@hacek u\or\py@grave u\else u%
    \fi
    \fontdimen5\font\dimen@ii
  }}

\def\py@tune@i#1{%
  \ifcase#1
    \or\py@macron \i\or\py@acute \i\or\py@hacek \i\or\py@grave \i\else i%
  \fi
}
\makeatletter
% End of pinyin

Multiple cursors allow you to have more than one active cursor in your text editor at once, which can be very useful for editing multiple lines simultaneously. Below are some examples of how to achieve this in Emacs and Vim:In Emacs:Emacs has a package called multiple-cursors that you can use for this purpose.Installation:You need to have the package installed. You can add it via MELPA or ELPA.Once installed, you need to require it in your Emacs config file:emacsCopy code(require 'multiple-cursors)
Usage Examples:mc/mark-next-like-this: Add another cursor to the next line that matches the current line.mc/mark-previous-like-this: Add another cursor to the previous line that matches the current line.mc/mark-all-like-this: Add a cursor to all lines in the buffer that match the current line.In Vim:Vim doesn't have built-in support for multiple cursors, but you can achieve similar functionality with visual block mode and plugins.Visual Block Mode:Press Ctrl + V to enter visual block mode.Move the cursor to select multiple lines.Press Shift + I to insert text, type the text you want to insert, and then press Esc.To replace or append text, you can use the c or A commands respectively after selecting lines in visual block mode.Using Plugins:Plugin like vim-multiple-cursors can be used to get behavior similar to Emacsâ multiple cursors.Installation can be done with your favorite plugin manager, like Vundle, Plug, or Pathogen.Once installed, you can use Ctrl + N to create new cursors at each occurrence of the word under the cursor.Example Workflow:In Emacs, you might use mc/mark-all-like-this to select all occurrences of a word and then type to replace them all at once.In Vim, you might use visual block mode to select a column of text and then insert, replace, or append text to all lines in the column simultaneously. Alternatively, you might use the vim-multiple-cursors plugin to select and edit multiple occurrences of a word.Consideration:Remember to consult the documentation for each package or plugin, as there are often additional features and commands available.Vim purists often use native features like visual mode, search and replace, or macros to achieve similar results without plugins.Before relying heavily on these features, itâs worth considering the different philosophies and workflows encouraged by Emacs and Vim, as well as your personal preferences and the specific requirements of your editing tasks.1 / 1You know you can just use byobu and send a message to all panes or all windows, let's say you were editing ten or twenty different documents...1 / 1ChatGPTIndeed, byobu is a powerful tool that provides text-based window management and terminal multiplexing. It allows users to have multiple terminal sessions within a single terminal window or remote terminal session, and it supports both tmux and screen as backend.You can broadcast your keystrokes to all panes or windows which is useful when you need to edit or execute similar commands on multiple sessions at once.Hereâs a general guide on how to use byobu to send messages to all panes or windows:Sending Message to All Panes in Byobu:Open byobu terminal.Split into multiple panes as needed using F2 to create new windows, Shift+F2 to create horizontal panes, and Ctrl+F2 to create vertical panes.Navigate between panes using Shift+Arrow Keys or Ctrl+Arrow Keys.Press Alt+Shift+F9 to enable input to all panes. Once this mode is activated, whatever you type in one pane will be sent to all panes.When youâre done, press Alt+Shift+F9 again to disable input to all panes.Sending Message to All Windows:Press Alt+F9 to enable input to all windows. This will broadcast your input to all windows in the byobu session.Type your command or text.Press Alt+F9 again to disable input to all windows.Considerations:Be careful while using broadcast input, especially when executing commands, as it might lead to unexpected behaviors if you are not aware of the context in each pane or window.The keybindings mentioned might vary depending on your byobu configuration and the backend (screen or tmux) that you are using. Refer to byobu's documentation or use byobu-keybindings command to view the current keybindings on your system.Itâs important to understand that while byobu and similar tools provide great convenience, the way they handle multiple cursors across different panes or windows is quite different from the multiple cursors feature within a single file in editors like Emacs or Vim. These are different tools designed for different tasks, and your choice will depend on your specific needs and workflow.1 / 1I think I sent a command to a dozen computers and about 20 different
